SNELI's sales in the Kivu region to its local consumers are projected to
increase from 52 GWh to 104 GWh during the 1986-1995 period, an overall
average annual increase of 8.0%.  Considering that in the recent past the
demand for electricity in this region grew at about 10% per year excluding
special industrial loads (para. 2.14), and that there is substantial
unserved demand, particularly in Goma, the forecast is reasonable. SNEL
will also continue to export electrical energy to Rwanda and Burundi as
discussed in para. 2.17.
Zaire (Kivu)-Burundi-Rwanda Regional Inzerconnected System
2.17        In examining the electric energy needs of the Kivu region of
Zaire, it is necessary to take the demand for Rwanda and Burundi into
consideration as well.  The interconnection of the electrical networks of
the three ccuntries is being strengthened with the construction of
Ruzizi II Project. A forecast of the availability of supply and demand for
electrical energy in the regional interconnected system 's given in



-19-
Annex  2.10.    The  demand  forecast  for  the  interconnected  system  is
equivalent to an average annual increase in demand of 9.42 during the
1986-1995 period. Review of these supply and demand forecasts leads to the
following conclusions:
A. From the regional (Burundi-Rwanda-Zaire (Kivu)) point of view:
(a) Energy from the Ruzizi II project will be required to supply the
regional needs beginning in 1989 (expected commissioning date
end 1988);
(b) the third unit (13.8 MW) of the Ruzizi II should be commissioned
by end-199?; and
(c) a new regional project would need to be commissioned ioy mid-1995.
B. From the point of view of the Kivu region of Zaire:
(a) following commissioning of the Rwegura (Burundi) and Ruzizi II
(Regional) power stations, the regional interconnected system
-particularly Burundi-is expected to have an oversupply of
electric power from the interconnected system until end-1993; 7/
this will limit exports from Zaire in 1989 and 1990;
(b) however, by 1995, Zaire (Kivu) exports are expected to increase
to a level to use all the surplus capacity; and
(c) Burundi will start using its share of Rrzizi II in 1988 and will
need to use more than its share startl-g in 1994; i.e. it will
become a net importer from Zaire.
2.18        The ability of the three national utilities (SNEL in Zaire,
ELECTROGAZ in Rwanda, and REGIDESO in Burundi) to absorb this surplus by
extending the interconnected grid to other regional towns is limited by the
availability of capital, both in foreign and local currency, and the
economic and financial viability of serving the demand, in all three
countries. The IDA Rwanda Power Prc4ect (CR 1495-RW, approved on June 12,
1984), the IDA Burundi Power Transmission and Distribution Project (CR
1593-BU, approved on May 9, 1985) and the proposed project would each
provide funds to construct new transmission lines and to rehabilitate and
extend the distribution networks, thereby expanding the interconnected grid
power consumption. However, further investment will likely be required as
well as the promotion of electric energy e.g. for cooking.   This will be
addressed in the preparation of IDA-assisted least-cost development plans
for each of the countries.
7/ Without Rwegura, it would not have been possible in Burundi to teet
daily peak demands and the energy requirements from 1987 onwards until
the Ruzizi II Project is commissioned.



-20-
Need for the Project
2.19        Rehabilitation and Extension of the Kivu Network. During the
preparation of the Ruzizi II Project it was found that Ruzizi I was in need
of rehabilitation. Inspections in 1984 and 1985, by consultants confirmed
this and identified works to be carried out.  The consultants determined
that the rehabilitation of the power station was the least-cost method for
the Zaire (Kivu)/Burundi/Rwanda interconnected system of generating the
energy which is now being produced in Ruzizi I.   In spite of excess
capacity in the period 1988-1992, rehabilitation of the power station is
necessary as degradation of the plant will result in its being unusable.
Existing transmission and distribution networks have not been maintained
properly because of lack of funds, both local and toreign, and also because
of the difficult political situation which prevailed in the region
following the independence of Zaire. In addition, consultants also studied
the possibility of extending the system to provide service to potential new
consumers in the areas surrounding the towns of the region and found that
these extensions would be justified (Annex 4.1).
2.20        Supplemental Rehabilitation of the Shaba Network.   The Shaba
Power System Rehabilitation Project was designed based on a 1980 study of
the physical conditions cf the generating plants and network in the Shaba
Region. It was recognized that the study could not predict the totality of
works needed once the units of the four power stations were opened and
provision was made under the project for a fund for unforeseen repairs of
about US$1.29 million. Works are now well advanced and have revealed the
need for supplementary rehabilitation works and replacements in excess of
the original estimate. These works are included in the proposed project in
view of the need to complete rehabilitation as soon as possible to ensure a
reliable supply of power to the mining industry (para 4.05).
2.21          Urgent Repairs and Operational  Improvements  for the Inga
Complex.   The operation of Inga I, Inga II and the Inga-Shaba line as
separate facilities rather than a synchronized system, plus the over design
of Inga II and the Inga-Shaba line have posed technical problems since
their commissioning.   Remedial actions by the original constructors and
efforts by operating personnel have sustained day-to-day operations, but
not without loss of efficiency and reliability, and some deterioration to
the plants.   In mid-1985 IDA recommended an independent study:  (i) to
correct the operating problems and establish rehabilitation and maintenance
procedures which would improve system reliability; and (ii) to develop a
long-term strategy which would eliminate the technical problems of
operation with excess  capacity.    Funds were  reallocated  under  Credit
1224-ZR  to finance  on  an emergency basis  a panel of  experts  for a
multi-phase independent study.   The first phase (urgent and short-term
measures to ensure operating soundness and identification of long-term
studies) was completed during March 1986, and preliminary findings conveyed
in May 1986.  Recommendations included a series of emergency actions and
urgent works which are included in the proposed project (para. 4.05). A
comprehensive  program  responding  to  medium-term  rehabilitation  and
recommendations of additional studies proposed by the panel is being
considered for the proposed energy project under preparation.



-21-
Alternatives Considered by the Government and SNEL to Utilize the Surplus
Generation Capacity at Inga II
2.22       Zone Franche d'Inga (ZOFI).  The Government has unsuccessfully
tried  to  promote  energy-intensive  industrial  development  (aluminium,
ammonia) by offering promotional electricity rates (Annex 7.1). However,
as the Inga surplus approaches full utilization, the promotional rates
offered for ZOFI by the Government would be well below the LRMC and amount
to a subsidy to the consumers. ZOFI's role has been revised to a promoter
of general industrial development with low cost energy as one incentive.
During negotiations, agreement was obtained that prices for surplus power
sold from Inga II would be adjusted to reflect long-run marginal cost at
the time Inga's capacity is fully committed and investments in additional
facilities for the supply and delivery of electricity are required.
2.23      Accelerated Electrification of Kinshasa.  One of the stated goals
of the Government is to make electricity available to about 70% of
Kinshasa's population by 1991. The Government expects, with this program,
to alleviate pressure on deforestation due to the concentrated demand by
Kinshasa's 200,000 households market for fuelwood (mainly charcoal) by
substituting surplus hydroelectricity for charcoal for cooking purposes.
As a first stage, the Government proposed to increase the number of
low-voltage connections in Kinshasa from 60,000 to 150,000 during the
1985-1988 period, mostly among low and middle-income families. The initial
phase, comprising 40,000 connections, is in progress (para. 2.13) but has
experienced difficulties due to the high cost of internal wiring (not
included in the program) and the inability of the Government to support the
cost of  subsidized  connections.    Preliminary analysis  indicates  that
substantial cost reductions could be made by decreasing design standards.
The Government has requested Bank Group assistance in reviewing the
technical, economic and financial aspects of the program and this review
will be linked to household energy studies under the project.
2.24       The scale and timing of the Kinshasa electrification program as
proposed by the Government (three years) also appear unrealistic given
Zaire's economic situation and the technical and financial capacity of SNEL
and/or the Government to implement such a program.  During negotiations,
agreement was obtained that during preparation of SNEL's long-term
development plan (para. 3.13), the timing and financial implications of the
accelerated electrification program of Kinshasa on SNEL and the Government
would be examined to determine the optimal phasing of the program and to
limit investment in accordance with that phasing; IDA, the Government and
SNEL would exchange views and agree on the best way to proceed with the
program.   In order to assist SNEL and the Government in determining the
feasibility of assumptions on household electricity use, the proposed
project includes a study of urban household energy needs, supplies and
substitutabilities (para. 4.05).
2.25      Conversion of Gas Oil and Fuel-Oil Fired Industrial Boilers and
Furnaces  to Electricity.   SNEL is also encouraging the conversion of
industrial boilers and furnaces in Kinshasa and other cities served by



-22-
Inga II to reduce the consumption of gas oil and fuel oil and increase that
of electric power. The additional demand for power would be about 100 MW
nationwide (500 GWh/year), most of it concentrated in the Kinshasa area.
SNEL is considering a price which would not exceed either the medium
voltage rate or the equivalent gas oil or fuel oil costs during the period
of boiler investment amortization (six to seven years) and rejoin the MV
tariff in effect after that period. A tariff based on this principle would
exceed the short-run cost of delivered power and also meet long-run pricing
objectives as long as MV power is priced to reflect its economic cost.
2.26       Exports to Congo.  According to current forecasts, Congo will
continue to import about 90 GWh/year from Zaire until 1991, to meet the
demand of Brazzavile until 1987 and the demand of both Brazzaville and
Pointe Noire, thereafter, during the dry season. According to the Congo's
own investment program installed capacity is expected to increase after
1991, limiting the potential for export (decreasing to about 25 GWh/year,
by 1995).  However, the Power Sector Memorandum dated September 1984 for
the People's Republic of the Congo (PRC), recommended that the PRC should
postpone costly investment in new generation projects and take advantage of
the large quantity of energy available from Zaire at an attractive price
(FCFA 5-7/kWh; USt1.3-1.8/kWh depending on the quantity) while maintaining
back-up capacity to preserve a degree of independence, as the power supply
from Zaire appears to be the least-cost solution for Brazzaville.  In 1985,
the two countries initiated discussions on the construction of a 220 kV,
300 km high voltage transmission line from Inga to Pointe Noire, which is
the port and main industrialized area of PRC.  As both countries would
gain, the Bank Group would encourage through its sector dialogue the
expansion of Zaire's exports on the basis of a price for power beneficial
to both parties.
Options Considered by the Government and SNEL to Increase the
Utilization of the Inga-Shaba Transmission System
2.27      Tapping the SIS at Kananga.  The city of Kananga, with a popula-
tion of about 450,000, near which the line passes, and Mbuji-Mayi, 150 km
away from the  line, are most obvious candidates for tapping.   Their
combined potential demand may well be around 20 MW but it is not possible
to estimate it accurately on the basis of present consumption, given the
current suppressed demand resulting from inadequate supply.   This option
would also increase the utilization of the Inga II power station. A major
difficulty, however, is that the tapping technology has not had enough
practical application anywhere in the world.   On the other hand,  for
Kananga, two nearby hydropower sites, namely Katende I (6.6 MW) and Katende
II (24 MW) have been identified, and the increase in demand in Mbuji-Mayi
could be supplied by three additional units of 1.1 MW each to be installed
by SNEL at the Lubilanji II hydropower plant presently being built by a
local mining company. It is therefore recommended that SNEL should execute
a three-pronged strategy to serve the needs of the region: in the short
term, rehabilitate and/or increase the efficiency of the diesel stations
now in operation at Kananga and Mbuji-Mayi; in the medium term, construct
the least-cost of the identified hydro projects; and in the longer term,



-23-
reassess the merits of tapping, based on technological and economic
analyses.    The Katende I Project and the units at Lubilanji II are
presently included in SNEL's draft development plan.  During negotiations
agreement was obtained that the study for the long-term options for the SIS
(Annex 4.1) would also deteruine whether follow up work for a tapping
station would be useful.
2.28       Exports to Zimbabwe.  In theory, exports of power to Zimbabwe,
chrough Zambia, could also increase the utilization of the SIS as all three
countries are already interconnected. However, with the present state of
the very weak growth of demand for electricity in Zambia and Zimbabwe,
existing and projected power surpluses in both countries and the other
supply alternatives available (e.g. rehabilitation of plants in Zimbabwe),
this option appears to be remote, at least in the medium-term. It may be
of longer-term interest, however, and should be considered in the context
of  regional  long-term planning  (Zaire/Zambia/Zimbabwe).    The Bank is
currently working with Zimbabwe on the preparation of its least-cost
development program.
III. TEE BORROWER AND THE IMPLEMENTING AGENCY
The Borrower
3.01       The Borrower would be the Republic of Zaire which would onlend
US$36.9  million  equivalent  to  the  Societe  Nationale  d'Electricite
(SNEL), the project implementing agency. US$0.1 million equivalent would
finance a study of urban household energy needs and alternative supply
options; the study would be supervised by SNEL on behalf of the Ministry of
Mines and Energy.
SNEL
3.02      SNEL is a Government-owned public enterprise which was originally
established in 1970 with responsibility for the construction of the Inga I
hydroelectric generating station.   In 1974, the Government dissolved the
six existing private power companies and transferred their assets,
liabilities and responsibilities to SNEL.  SNEL was effectively recreated
in its present form by Ordinance 78-196 dated May 5, 1978, which gives SNEL
the authority necessary to discharge its responsibility for the generation,
transmission and distribution of electricity throughout Zaire. In December
1978, SNEL took over the electric generating and distribution facilities
and operations of REGIDESO, the Government-owned water utility which in
addition to its water supply operations also sold electricity to consumers
in urban areas, where it generated electricity for its water supply and
pumping operations.
3.03       SNEL operates under the supervision of three Ministries (Mines
and Energy, Finance and Portfolio) through a ten member Board of Directors
appointed by the President of the Republic. The chairman of the Board is
the Director General (President Delegue General-PDG), a full-time chief



-24-
executive responsible for overall management of the company. The Board is
comprised of SNEL's Deputy Director General (Delgue Genfral Adjoint-DGA)
and technical and financial/administrative directors, representatives of
the Ministry of Mines and Energy, Ministry of Finance, Bank of Zaire, and
REGIDESO and two independent members. The Board meets at least every two
months. Since 1981, when IDA lending to SNEL was initiated, the Board has
taken prompt and effective decisions regarding proposals for tariff
adjustments and restructuring of the organization, both of which were key
elements of  the IDA/SNEL dialogue.   While in principle  the Board is
responsible for all decisions relating to SNEL's operational and financial
performance, tariff adjustments are subject to Government approval and in
the 1970s major investment decisions were taken by the Government without
due regard for their future impact on SNEL (para. 3.14).   A management
committee comprising the PDG, DGA, two directors, and a workers'
representative are responsible for the day-to-day management of SNEL.
3.04       Provision has been made for internal accounting controls, but
these have not been effective except for the policing of cash transactions
in regional offices. The management assistance program (para. 3.16) is in
the process  of establishing an internal audit unit.   A three member
external audit commission (CollAge des Commissaires aux Comptes), which
reports to the Minister of Finance, has the right to examine all of SNEL's
financial  activities  and  operations  and  give  an  opinion  on  the
representativeness  of  SNEL's  accounts.    While  this  follows  standard
practice for parastatals in Zaire, it has not been effective or produced
useful results in general owing to the scarcity of adequately trained
accountants  and  auditors.    SNEL  has  therefore  appointed  independent
external auditors for the auditing of its accounts in accordance with IDA
stipulations (para. 3.11).
Organization and Management
3.05       SNEL's organization chart is shown in Annex 3.1.  The present
PDG, a Zairian national, was appointed to his position in 1980 and has
proved to be competent and effective in working towards improvement in
SNEL's performance.   During the last part of 1982, SNEL restructured its
organization to replace the previous horizontal pattern-in which fourteen
department directors reported to the management committee-with a pyramidal
hierarchy. In April 1985, the general management was strengthened by the
creation of the position of the Deputy director general (DGA), however, the
position is presently vacant.   Three positions are immediately under the
PDG and DGA: two managing directors, one in charge of finance, personnel
and aaministration (an expatriate) 4ncluding sales management, the other (a
Zaire national) in charge of the techiuical orerations and construction of
projects; and, a general manager (a Zaire national) in charge of all
aspects of operations in the seven regions.Compared with the previous
structure  which  was  inefficient  due   to  excessive   diffusion  of
responsibilities, the new structure has improved communication channels 3nd
clarified responsibility.   Further changes in the structure are being
considered to reduce the over-centralization of authority; SNEL has
established  an  Organization  and  Methods  Committee  (OMC)  to  define



-25-
guidelines to identify, train or recruit competent managers for the
eventual decentralization. OMC is being assisted by management consultants
(Sema-Metra, France and Sobemap, Belgium) under the institutional
assistance activities of CR 1224-ZR (para. 3.16).
3.06       SNEL has its head office in Kinshasa and is organized into six
geographical regions (Kinshasa, Western (Bas Zaire), Northern, Central,
Southern (Shaba) and Eastern (including Kivu)) and one administrative
region- manag_ng the operations of the Inga-Shaba transmission system
(SIS).  The organization of the Eastern Region which includes the Kivu
network is typical of SNEL's regional structures in that it comprises a
regional office in Kisangani which is largely autonomous in its technical
management of the operations of the local hydro and diesel plants and
distribution.   However, decisions on personnel and finance are taken by
headquarters.   The Kivu subregion is in charge of the operation of the
Ruzizi I hydropower plant and exports to Rwanda and Burundi.  Financial
control is exercised by the head office in Kinshasa, including accounting
and centralized bank account. The Kivu local staff and management (Zairian
nationals except for foreman in charge of the Ruzizi I-Bujumbura line) are
competent; operations have been carried out without major problems; power
failures, average for a system of that age, have been mainly due to
shortages of materials and replacement equipment requiring foreign
exchange.
Personnel
3.07         The present profile of SNEL staff reflects a low level of
training and skills at the time of recruitment limiting the basic
theoretical knowledge essential for fully effective execution of tasks.
Performance is further constrained by shortages of tools and equipment in
operating units.   Staff motivation has suffered from these constraints,
inadequate remuneration and the perceived absence of career prospects. In
the context of SNEL's general management improvement program (para. 3.16)
which is being financed under CR 1224-ZR, SNEL is reviewing an incentive
system to improve staff performance.   Upgrading of SNEL staff would be
supported through assistance to the Sanga traning center under the
proposed project (Annex 4.1).   Materials and tools to rehabilitate the
center would also be supplied.
3.08        At the end of 1985, SNEL employed a total of 4,697 staff to
supply 116,509 consumers-an average of one employee per 25 consumers. In
view of the diverse nature of SNEL's operations, which include diesel
installations, hydro generating stations and a number of scattered isolated
systems and the geographical dispersion, the ratio of consumers per
employee does not appear to be excessive in comparison with other Eastern
and Southern African countries.   As shown in Annex 3.2, there are 946
cadres (managers and university graduates) and skilled technicians, and
3,751 unskilled workers. The implementation of SNEL's new organizational
structure (para. 3.05) streamlined employment at SNEL by reducing unskilled
staff.   The number of employees fell from 5,200 in 1980 to 4,697 in
December 1985. It is expected that savings being achieved will be utilized
to remunerate staff for good performance thereby creating better incentives
and the possibility of career advancement.



-26-
3.09      The number of expatriate staff declined steadily during the last
10 years from 67 in 1985 to 30 in 1986. Lower technician levels have also
been filled by Zairians while the remaining expatriates are in key
managerial positions in the areas of management of power plants and
transmission lines, and accounting, co-nercial, administrative and computer
operations. However, higher expatriate technician positions have also been
filled by advisers obtained through bilateral technical assistance programs
in form of grants.   Presently 13 advisers, financed through bilateral
assistance programs, are employed by SNEL.8/ SNEL is reliant to a large
degree on c -nsultants, especially for its financial, commercial, project
studies, design and procurement activities. The training of counterparts
has not received adequate attention because of the emphasis by expatriates
and consultants on carrying out day-to-day responsibilities to keep SNEL
operating.   The objective  of progressively decreasing  the number of
consultants and replacing them with Zairians would receive more attention
under the training activities of the proposed project and the management
assistance program being implemented under CR 1224-ZR and the proposed
project (paras. 3.16 and 4.05).
SNEL Performance
3.10       The Bank Group's first operation with SNEL was the Shaba Power
System Rehabilitation Project which was approved on April 1, 1982
(para.  1.10).    This project  supports  rehabilitation of hydroelectric
generators which are the primary power source for GECAMINES as well as
other consumers of the Shaba Region. Because of the emergency nature of
the operation, the project limited its focus on performance indicators of
SNEL's Southern Region (which includes Shaba) and identified general
SNEL management and operational weaknesses for which further study and
direct technical support from consultants were proposed (para. 3.16).
Implementation of the physical works of the project were delayed by with-
drawal of a cofinancier and delays in the contract award, but are now being
executed  reasonably  well.       Institutional  development  progress  is
encouraging  owing   to  the  receptiveness  of  SNEL's  management  to
recommendations on reorganization and streamlining of procedures, although
staff training has lagged behind because of limited resources and
preoccupation with day-to-day operations. The financial performance of the
Southern Region in isolation from SNEL's overall activities has been
consistently good: tariff adjustments have been adequate to meet covenanted
rates of return (4% in 1983, 6% in 1984 and 8% in 1985) and a separate
accounting region was created for the government-financed Inga-Shaba System
(SIS) (para. 3.06).   The Government's decision in 1983 to end separate
treatment of the SIS and transfer the Inga-Shaba line and Inga II
hydrostation to SNEL is supported by IDA in principle, but will have a
negative impact on SNEL's financial situation in the medium to longer
term.   SNEL's recent financial performance and the implications of the
asset transfer are discussed in Chapter V.
8/ Three French advisors, 8 Belgian advisors, one Egyptian advisor, and
one Yugoslav advisor are provided through bilateral assistance program.



-27-
Accounting and Audits
3.11        SNEL's accounting department is under the supervision of the
Administrative and Financial Director. Accounts are kept centrally for the
head office, seven regions (para. 3.06) plus four sub-regions (three in the
Southern (Shaba) region and one in the Eastern (Kivu) region).   In the
context of the Shaba Power System Rehabilitation Project (CR. 1224-ZR),
deficiencies in SNEL's accounts were identified resulting from a shortage
of adequately trained staff, the change to a new accounting system in 1979,
and a lack of financial discipline. In 1980, HElios of France, financed by
the CCCE, began working with SNEL to improve its financial management and
to audit its accounts; in 1983 Helios also initiated a revaluation of
SNEL's assets. Additional assistance is being received under the general
management program financed by CR 1224-ZR (para. 3.16) which aims at
strengthening SNEL's operating capability in several areas including
finance. A limitet' audit of SNEL's accounts was carried out in 1980, and
in compliance w'   conditions established under CR 1224-ZR, annual audits
have been and will continue to be undertaken bf an independent auditor
(CHlios) and submitted to IDA. As CCCE's financing for SNEL's audits ended
in 1984, the proposed project will provide the required foreign exchange
for the 1985-1987 audits. SNEL's 1981-1983 audits were qualified; the 1984
audit received certification with qualification and the 1985 audit is
expected to be completed by September 1986. While improvements have been
noted by Helios in the areas of inter-regional coordination, billing of HV
and MV clients and some accounting practices, problems leading to
qualification of the accounts have been cited in the areas of internal
control, inventory management and the qualifications of accounting staff-
Major revisions to SNEL's accounts included in 1984 correction of anomalies
following recommendations of the auditing, and in 1985 the transfer of
major assets at their value in use and a revaluation of all assets (paras.
3.14 and 5.04).  SNEL is making efforts through the general management
assistance program to improve the standards of its accounting practices.
Insurance
3.12       Insurance in the past, apart from statutory insurance, has only
covered freight and transport of goods as required of contractors employed
by SNEL. SNEL's own risks have been covered on the basis of self insurance
without making any provision for an insurance fund. During negotiations,
agreement was reached to review this policy under the management assistance
program with a view to providing suitable insurance coverage for SNEL's
assets. SNEL does not carry or have not carried out systematic inspections
of its dams. However, the movements of the Nzilo dam in the Shaba region
are being studied by Hydro-Quebec International of Canada, financed from CR
1224-ZR. The Ruzizi I dam was inspected within the feasibility studies of
the proposed project (Annex 4.1).
Investment Planning and Programming
3.13      Systematic planning for the power sector was lacking in the past
in part due to a shortage of qualified staff and expertise and also to a



-28-
lack of strong commitment to the planning concept by the Government.
CR 1224-ZR is financing assistance to SNEL for the preparation of a
long-term development plan to the year 2000.  Exchange of views is being
carried out within the supervision of CR 1224-ZR and preparation of a
proposed energy project. In addition to the new projects, the plan will
include a systematic audit of SNEL's diesel and isolated hydro plant
operations  and  recommendations  on:       (i)  rehabilitating  (including
maintenance needs) the existing small hydro and diesel plants which supply
isolated areas; (ii) extending these plants; and (iii) substituting the
diesel plants with new hydro plants.  During negotiations it was agreed
that the draft of the plan would be completed by September 30, 1986 and
furnished to IDA for an exchange of views. It was also agreed that IDA and
SNEL would exchange views annually on the revisions of this plan until June
30, 1990.  Before undertaking any investment exceeding the equivalent of
US$5 million, the Government and SNEL would furnish for the Association's
approval a justification that the investment is least-cost and has an
assured financing plan which spells out SNEL's and Government's obligations
for financial charges, including debt service, operation, maintenance and
depreciation.   Awaiting  the conclusions of the development plan,  the
Government, SNEL and IDA agreed on an indicative investment program which
reflects reasonable growth in demand for electricity, the availability of
local and foreign funds and conforms to the expected macroeconomic
situation in Zaire. The total costs (base costs, and physical and price
contingencies) of this modified investment *program which covers the
1986-1992 period is estimated at Z 59.7 billion (equivalent to US $693
million) of which Z 49.8 billion (equivalent to US $581 million) is in
foreign currency. SNEL's investment program is given in Annex 3.3.
3.14        In the past, the Government has intervened in the planning
process and carried out under its own financing large infrastructure
investments including the Inga II hydroplant, Inga-Shaba line and Shaba
high voltage line.   These investments were based on overly optimistic
demand projections which have not materialized, resulting in the case of
Inga II and the SIS in substantial capacity underutilization (about 14%
utilization for Inga II and about 24% for the SIS). SNEL has operated the
line and the plant on the Government's behalf since their commissioning in
1982/83; however, ownership, debt service and maintenance charges for
the Inga-Shaba line and debt service for Inga II have remained with the
Government. In 1983, the Government decided that the plant and the line
should become SNEL's assets, although no legal transfer has taken place.
Debt service, operating and maintenance costs of these investments could
not be- borne by consumers without subsidy if all associated costs are also
transferred to SNEL.   This would also represent a long-term burden for
SNEL'.; financial situation since capacity utilization is not expected to
increase above 50% for Inga II by 1991 and may even decline in the case of
SIS as demand in the Shaba region is once again served by local hydropower
stations now under rehabilitation (para. 2.08). As revenues generated from
the assets accrue to SNEL, it is proposed that SNEL finance operating and
maintenance costs of the plant and the line and that portion of the debt
service corresponding to the utilized capacity of Inga II. SNEL and the
Government are in the process of defining legal and financial



-29-
responsibility for the majority of the assets now operated by SNEL and it
is proposed that in the context of this agreement the Government finalize
the transfer of Inga II and the SIS based on their value in use: 302 of
replacement cost for Inga II, and zero for the Inga Shaba line for which
there is limited need given the generating capacity already available in
the Shaba region and a lesser cost alternative to increase supply when
existing capacity is fully utilized. Projected financial statements given
in Annexes 5.1-5.4 introduce these assets as revalued and at their value in
use and assume increases in capacity utilization for Inga II to attain 50Z
by 1991. During negotiations, agreement was reached that SNEL's accounts
would be adjusted to reflect the transfer of Inga II and the SIS at their
value in use in accordance with accounting practices acceptable to IDA.
Legal Transfer of Assets
3.15          The only assets to which SNEL has clear title are those
constituting its original capital, i.e. the assets of the seven former
private companies dissolved in 1974 (para. 3.02). Nearly all investments
undertaken since then have been financed by the Government and are being
operated by  SNEL.    In addition  to a lack of clarity in the legal
arrangements, this situation prevents SNEL from setting its electricity
rates to adequately operate, maintain and renew the majority of assets in
the power sector. SNEL has initiated discussions with the Government on an
agreement which would clarify respective legal and financial objectives and
broaden  the  objectives  of  its  tariff  policy.    During  negotiations,
agreement was reached that SNEL and the Government conclude by June
30, 1987 a legal agreement to (i) determine ownership of all assets
financed by the Government but which are operated by SNEL; (ii) establish
responsibility for payment of existing debt service until all outstanding
loans are fulLy repaid; (iii) define the broad objectives of SNEL's tariff
policy such that SNEL can cover from its own resources operation and
maintenance costs and renewal and expansion of its assets; and, (iv)
transfer the Inga II hydroplant and Inga Shaba line to SNEL at a transfer
price based on their value in use (para. 3.14).   During negotiations,
agreement was also obtained that beginning in 1987, SNEL would cover from
its own resources all operating and maintenance charges associated with the
Inga II hydroplant and Inga Shaba transmission line and reimburse over a
ten-year period a portion of the original debt related to construction of
the Inga II hydroplant corresponding to its value in use.
Institutional Assistance to SNEL
3.16          To assist SNEL in upgrading its management capabilities,
substantial institutional assistance has been provided under CR.1224-ZR.
As part of this program, several studies and assistance activities have
been launched including an analysis of electricity tariff issues, a study
of asset revaluation, establishment of a planning unit, and rehabilitation
and improvement of the data management unit and computer system used for
data analyses, accounting and budgeting. The tariff study was completed in
mid-1985; asset revaluation will be completed by mid-1986; and the planning
unit was started in May 1984 (para. 3.13).   The data management study,



-30-
which started in November 1982, was initially intended to be directed
mainly to computer problems, but was extended with IDA's approval to a
general management assistance program.  A review of technical assistance
received recently by SNEL was undertaken by a joint IDA/CCCE mission in
March 1986. In addition to a general evaluation,9/ the mission identified
the major problems SNEL encountered with technical assistance programs and
prepared  recommendations  to  assist  SNEL  in  finding  solutions.    The
conclusion of the evaluation was that many positive results had been
achieved since intensive management and organizational assistance was
introduced in 1982, but that execution of new programs and systems had
experienced setbacks because of a lack of physical and human resources.
Actions taken in the 1982-1985 period are described in Annex 3.4.   The
second phase of the general management assistance which began under CR
1224-ZR will be extended under the proposed project in the areas of
personnel management, procurement and inventory control, accounting and
internal control procedures and will be directed towards two axes: (i)
consolidation of the basic information and management systems; and (ii)
dynamization of SNEL through planning, responsibility, motivation and
training. Intensification of human resource development activities will
also be undertaken to develop a long-term training plan and initiate
manpower planning.   During negotiations agreement was reached with SNEL
that it would: (i) obtain within the proposed project (para. 4.05 and
Annex 4.1) the services of eight qualified experts for a period of two
years; (ii) prepare by July 31, 1986, an interim action plan for the
resumption of training activities for technical personnel as well as
managers, consult with IDA on its results and no later than September 1,
1986, implement the plan as agreed with IDA; and (iii) reinforce the
existing institutional assistance for human resources to develop a Training
Master Plan which will be completed in draft form and furnished to IDA for
comments by November 1, 1986.
IV. THE PROJECT
Preparation of the Project
4.01      Rehabilitation and Extension Needs in the Kivu Region.  Following
the initiation of the Ruzizi II Regional Hydroelectric Project (para. 1.11)
and with the prospect of a significant increase in the amount of electric
power available to the Kivu region of Zaire (para. 2.17), the Government is
proceeding with the rehabilitation and extension of the transmission and
distribution  facilities  and  also  rehabilitation  of  the  Ruzizi  I
hydrostation  to  make  optimal  use  of  power  within  the  regional
interconnected system.   Burundi and Rwanda have taken similar parallel
steps with IDA assistance (para. 2.18).   IDA received and subsequently
approved on May 10, 1983 a request from the Government of Zaire for an
advance from the Project Preparation Facility (PPF P246) in the amount of
US$440,000 to carry out the following studies in preparation for the
proposed project:
(a) feasibility of the rehabilitation needs of the Ruzizi I hydro-
power plant;
9/  This  evaluation  covered  the  financial  and  commercial  systems,
supply/purchasing, structure and organization, human resources and
training.



-31-
(b) feasibility of the rehabilitation and extension of the transmis-
sion and distribution network in the Kivu region; and
(c) feasibility study for the construction of a wood-fired plant at
Mbandaka in the Equateur (North) region.
SNEL retained the services of ICN which has completed its reports. On the
basis of the consultant's recommendations, the Government requested IDA
financing for the rehabilitation and expansion of the generation,
transmission and distribution facilities in the Kivu region. As a result,
a mission visited Zaire in November 1984 to appraise the proposed project.
In order to expedite the project, the Government requested that the PPF
advance be raised to US$1 million so that it could retain consultants for
the design, call for and analysis of tenders. The extension was approved
on October 1, 1985.
4.02        Wood-Fired Plant at Mbandaka.  During the preparation of the
project, IDA also agreed to include in PPF P246, the feasibility study for
the construction of a wood-fired power plant at Mbandaka in the Equateur
(North) region, because no feasible hydro site has been identified in the
area and a wood-fired station may be the least-cost option. Consultants
(EdF International) concluded in their report dated February 1975
(Annex 7.1) that a 6 MW wood-fired power station was not competitive with
respect to a diesel extension. 10/
4.03       Preparation of Supplemental Rehabilitation for the Shaba Power
System and Emergency Repairs for the Inga Complex.   Preparation was
undertaken during supervision of Credit 1224-ZR and is based on reports of
the consulting engineers (ACEC/Tractionel) and the panel of experts
(HydroQuebec) convened at the request of IDA (para. 2.08 and Annex 4.1).
Project Objectives and Relation to the Sector
4.04      The main objective of the project is to ensure a reliable supply
of electrical energy to the two main interconnected networks of
Inga-Bas Zaire-Shaba and the Kivu region. The project will also serve to
make use of electrical energy within the Zaire (Kivu)-Rwanda-Burundi inter-
connected system by increasing the transmission and distribution cape ity
of the network in the Kivu region where there is much suppressed deand and
to strengthen SNEL as an institutiorn through better management, plann'ng,
rational pricing, improved financial policies and training of it-s staff.
Project Description
4.05        The main features of the project are given in Annex 4.1 and
summarized as follows:
10/ The main reason for the negative conclusion is that the area studied
around the town of Mbandaka is particularly marshy and subject to
flooding. About 70% of the area is hydromorphus soil, unusable for the
exploitation of the natural forest and also for plantation.   This
weighed heavily on the operating costs.

I. Rehabilitation and extension works:
- rehabilitation of the Ruzizi I hydropower plant (complete
overhauling of the generating units, construction of stator
windings, relays, signalization);
- rehabilitation and expansion of the transmission and distribution
network in the Kivu region and interconnection with the Ruzizi II
110 kV tranamission network (rehabilitation of the 6.6 and 15 kV
distribution network and extension of the 15 kV lines in four
towns--Goma, Bukavu, Uvira, Kiliba-i.e. construction of about 83
km of new MV and 150 km of new LV lines; and construction of a 70
kV 17 Ikm antenna line from Ruzizi I-Bujumbura line and 70/15 kV 5
MVA substation for the supply of Kiliba and Uvira);

regulators, replacement of the shaft of the unit No. 4 (65 MW) at
Nseke, repairs and replacement of the valves at Nzilo and Nseke
dams);

Inga II hydropower facilities (supervision, procurement and
installation  of equipment and  spares  responding  to highest
priority needs over the next eighteen months);

SNEL (high frequency equipment to be installed at Kinshasa, Inga,
Lubumbashi, Bukavu and Kisangani):
II. Technical and institutional assistance to SNEL including studies

in personnel, financial, commercial, procurement, planning;
studies on revaluation of assets, audits, tariffs; preparation of
a contract for the transfer from the Government to SNEL of
ownership rights of assets financed and presently owned by the
Government but operated by SNEL; study on urban household energy
needs; employment of eight qualified experts); and,
III. Assistance for SNEL's training needs (rehabilitation of existing
facilities, continuation of services of the senior training
consultant, advance training of instructors at Sanga or abroad;
installation of equipment for training in the operation and
maintenance of diesel plants; Annex 4.2).
Cost Estimates
4.06        The total project cost is estimated to be US$41.9 million,
excluding duties and taxes, from which the project is exempt, and excluding
interest during construction. The foreign exchange component is estimated
to be US$37.6 million, or about 90% of the total project cost.   The
estimated cost of the principal components of the project are given in
detail in Annex 4.3 and summarized In the Credit and Project Summary.



-33-
Basis for Estimates
4.07      The cost estimates for the consulting services, technical assis-
tance and training have been prepared by IDA, while the costs of the other
components have been estimated by SNEL's consultants, ICM and Tractionel.
These cost estimates were reviewed by IDA and were found to be reasonable.
Base costs are in March 1986 price levels. Physical contingencies of 10%
were added to each component to provide an allowance for unforeseen
increases  in  the  volume  of  work.    The  Bank's  present  estimate  of
international price increases for manufactured goods was used for price
contingencies on foreign costs, as follows: 1986, 7.2%; 1987-1988 6.8%; and
1989: 7.0%. In view of the Government's flexible exchange rate policy, all
project costs have been expressed in US$ and the assumption made that the
progressive devaluation of the Zaire currency would compensate for p. ice
increases in local costs.
Financing Plan
4.08       The proposed IDA credit of US$37.0 million would finance about
88% of the estimated project cost of US$41.9 million and about 98% of the
estimated foreign currency expenses (US$37.6 million) of the project, in
both cases excluding interest during construction, which will be paid by
SNEL in local currency. The UNDP will finance part of the cost of training
activities (US$0.6 million). Interest during construction related to the
IDA Credit is estimated at US$6.5 million and will be financed by SNEL in
addition to all local currency expenditures (US$4.3 milion).   A summary
fundiag plan appears in the Credit and Project Summary.
4.09      The proceeds of the IDA Credit would be onlent to SNEL at 8.5%
for a period of 20 years including five years' grace. SNEL will assume the
foreign exchange risk. Conditions of Credit Effectiveness would be (i) the
execution of a subsidiary loan agreement 'tween SNEL and the Government;
and,  (ii)  the  execution  of  UNDP's  agi-ement making  the grant  funds
available to SNEL.
4.10          SNEL would finance through cash generation, local currency
requirements of about US$10.8 million equivalent (22% of the project total
cost, including IDC).
Status of Engineering and Implementation
4.11           SNEL would be responsible for the implementation of the
rehabilitation and extension components of the project and would be
assisted by engineering consultants. SNEL has signed engineering contracts
with ICM of Germany (the consultants for the initial feasibilitv studies;
para. 4.01) for rehabilitation of Ruzizi I and rehabilitation and expansion
of the Kivu transmission and distribution network; and with Tractionel of
Belgium for rehabilitation of the Shaba power system.   These consultants
are acceptable to IDA and during negotiations, agreement was reached that
SNEL would continue to employ consultants on terms and conditions
satisfactory to IDA and in accordance with the Bank Group guidelines for
the  use  of  consultants.    Physical  works  would  be  carried  out  by



-34-
contractors.    The preparation of  the  preliminary  designs  and  tender
documents  are  scheduled  to  be  completed  by  September  1,  1986,
rehabilitation and extension of the Kivu distribution network by end-1988
and rehabilitation of the Shaba power system and the Ruzizi I Power Plant
and by end-1989 as shown on the implementation schedule (Annex 4.4). These
schedules appear reasonable in view of the fact that the work to be
performed does not require construction of major structures.  Bids have not
yet been received.    However,  as  the contracts will  include  commonly
purchased material and equipment, and erection services would be routine in
nature, riskz of having cost overruns are estimated to be small.
Procurement
4.12          Societe Nationale de Trading.   The Government,  aware of
procurement problems in all its public enterprises, sought to address them
through the creation in March 1985 of a central procurement agencv, the
Societe Nationale de Trading (SONATRAD), to serve five large public
enterprises,  including  SNEL.11/       SONATRAD's  mandate  is  to  permit
substantial improvements in procurement through improved negotiation
techniques,   grouping   orders   from   several   public   enterprises,
standardization of common equipment, elimination of certain purchasing
intermediaries, diversification of the sources of supply, and promotion of
competitive local producers. Extensive discussions have taken place since
March 1985 between the Government, SONATRAD, SNEL, GECAMINES and the Bank
to develop SONATRAD into an institution that can eFfectively play its role
of improving the procurement practices of the public enterprises involved
and to clearly spell out in acceptable bilateral contracts the respective
roles and responsibilities of the public enterprises and SONATRAD.   A
Purchasing Agreement (Annex 7.1) signed on April 6, 1986 between SNEL and
SONATRAD and approved by the Government, elaborates SONATRAD's role in the
following areas: (1) to serve as SNEL's purchasing agent for a limited
number of large contracts (above US$3.0 million for 1986) and for contracts
of equipment common to sereral public enterprises and where substantial
savings can be expected from grouping of orders; (ii) to control and audit
SNEL's purchasing practices, with particular emphasis on commercial
intermediaries, sta-ndardization, and monopoly situations; and, (iii) to
advise SNEL on purchasing procedures, knowledge of the equipment market,
and generally upgrade SNEL's purchasing skills. The Government, SNEL and
SONATRAD have agreed to a review of the threshold every six months and for
assurances that it could not be changed without prior Bank's approval. The
Purchasing Agreement between SNEL and SONATRAD is a satisfactory document
which adequately addresses the weaknesses of the present system.   The
parties have also agreed that SNEL will monitor SONATRAD's performance as
its purchasing agent and that quarterly external audits would apprise SNEL
and SONATRAD of the quality of implementation of the Purchasing Agreement.
4.13       General.  Some of the items to be purchased under the project,
particularly for the rehabilitation of the Ruzizi I and Shaba power plants
and at Inga I and Inga II power plants are proprietary in nature and can
only be supplied by the original manufacturer. Thus, it would be necessary
11/ GECAMINES, SNEL, REGIDESO, SNCZ, ONATRA.



-35-
for SNEL to negotiate directly with the original manufacturer for the
supply and guarantee for any installation of these types of equipment. The
total cost of items to be purchased in this manner is estimated to be
around US$5.0 million.   Nevertheless, attempts will be made to obtain as
broad a response as possible for the supply of this type of equipment, and
the possibility of requesting proposals for substituting equipment from
other suppliers will be investigated. This method was approved and applied
under CR 1224-ZR The general contractor for the installation and erection
works for the Shaba Power System Rehabilitation was appointed in accordance
with Bank guidelines.   Other materials and equipment, including erection
services, to be financed by the proposed IDA Credit would be purchased in
accordance with IDA's guidelines for international competitive bidding.
Procurement for cofinanced items of the project would be in accordance with
the colender's normal  practices.    Consultants  would  be  selected and
employed in accordance with principles and procedures satisfactory to IDA
on the basis of Bank's guidelines for the use of consultants whose
extension of service will be paid from the proposed Credit. Consultants in
charge were all selected in accordance with the Bank guidelines (e.g.
institutional assistance: Sema-Metra-Sobemap-para. 3.16; engineering for
the rehabilitation of the Shaba Power System: Tractionel-paras. 1.10 and
2.20; engineering for the Ruzizi I power plant and Kivu system:
ICM-para. 4.01).    Urgent rehabilitation needs of the hydroplants would
require that contracts be placed and some payments be made in advance of
credit effectiveness.    The  total amount  of  retroactive  financing  is
estimated at a maximum of about US$750,000.   A tabulation indicating the
method of procurement of the various components is given in Annex 4.5.
Disbursements
4.14        The proceeds of the IDA Credit would be disbursed over five
fiscal years as follows, to finance:
(a) repayment of the PPF advance (US$1.0 million) for the preliminary
engineering study and detailed design and preparation of contract
documents;
(b) 100% of the foreign costs of the engineering services, technical
assistance and studies (US$10.1 million);
(c) 100% of the foreign currency expenditures and 90% of local
expenditures financed contracts for materials and works for the
rehabilitation of the Ruzizi I, Shaba and Inga hydro plants
(US$12.2 million), rehabilitation and extension of the Kivu
transmission and distribution networks and Ruzizi II feeder
(US$11.2   million)    and    radio    communication    equipment
(US$0.09 million); and
(d) unallocated funds totalling US$2.41 million.
4.15      As the 17 km, 70 kV branch line to supply Kiliba and Uvira will
originate from a tower located in Burundi and a portion of this branch line



-36-
will be built in that country, it was agreed with SNEL that disbursements
for expenditures for the Uvira and Kiliba portions of the project would be
subject to the Government of Zaire and SNEL obtaining from the Government
of Burundi sufficient rights to permit free access to Burundi for the
construction, operation and maintenance of this branch line.
4.16       Claims relating to any contract or purchase order whose value is
less than US$20,000 will be submitted under statements of expenditures, the
documentation for which will be retained at SNEL headquarters and made
available for inspection by IDA supervision missions.   All other claims
will be fully documented.   The closing date for the credit would be
December 31, 1990.   The disbursement profile (Annex 4.6) differs from
standard profiles of average power projects since funding is provided
mainly for rehabilitation and extension of transmission and distribution
networks (a limited portion of a complete power project including
generation) and institutional and operational technical assistance to
SNEL.   The schedule is reasonable. A Special Account of US$1.0 million,
financed under the Project, would be established in an account to be opened
in a commercial bank for the purpose of alleviating SNEL's difficulty in
pre-financing expenditures to be reimbursed under the IDA Credit, and
operated under terms and conditions acceptable to IDA. The special account
would be replenished on a monthly basis on the basis of withdrawal
applications  submitted  by  SNEL  and  acceptable  to  IDA.    Should  any
disbursements be made from the special account which are not acceptable to
IDA, SNEL would deposit the corresponding amount into the Special Account.
Agreements on terms and conditions for using the Special Account were
reached at negotiations.
Project Monitoring
4.17        The records and reports necessary to monitor progress of the
project and its evaluation were agreed upon during negotiations.   The
proposed detailed guidelines for a project monitoring system are given in
Annex 4.7.  The project is expected to be completed by June 30, 1990.
Preparation of a project completion report not later than six months after
project completion was agreed during negotiations.
Environmental Considerations
4.18      The construction of the transmission and distribution facilities
would use commonly known and well-tried practices.   The effect on the
environment would be as minimal as in other areas of the country.
V. FINANCIAL ANALYSIS
Past and Present Situation
5.01      As noted in paragraph 3.11, SNEL's accounts and accounting system
have been the focus of extensive technical assistance intended to improve
internal consistency and control. An analysis of SNEL's audited 1984 and
unaudited 1985 results is given below, but should be interpreted with



-37-
caution since the 1984 accounts contain numerous revisions of anomalies
related to previous years based upon the auditors' recommendations and the
1985 results are based on preliminary results of an asset revaluation study
still under review by IDA, SNEL and the Government (para. 5.04).   SNEL
continues to receive assistance to improve its accounting practices.
5.02          Operating results for 1984 and  1985,  based  on available
accounting data, are summarized in Table 5.1.
5.03       The results of SNEL's operations for 1984 yield a rate of return
of 8.5% on net fixed assets. This rate of return is not representative of
SNEL's financial situation which is distorted by (i) the recording of most
of SNEL's assets at their historical costs, and (ii) the inadequate
depreciation charges for these assets.
5.04       An improvement in SNEL's cash generation in 1985 resulted from
several rate increases throughout the year.  However this improvement is
negated, producing a negative rate of return for 1985 of -1.2%, when
adjustments are introduced which: (i) revalue SNEL's assets to reflect
their utility value;12/ (ii) value the Inga II and the Inga-Shaba line
based on use (30% of replacement cost for Inga II and 0 for the Inga-Shaba
line (para. 3.14) rather than at the arbitrarily low value utilized in
1984; (iii) increase depreciation charges in accordance with the new asset
values, and (iv) incorporate substantial one-time adjustments to operating
costs recommended by the auditor and reflecting anomalies in earlier
accounts. Results for 1985 should be regarded with caution since they are
based on preliminary results of the Helios asset revaluation study which is
subject to modification following discussion with SNEL and the Government.
Review of the revaluation study will be completed by end 1986 and
incorporated in the accounts of that year, and finalization of asset
transfer will be completed by mid-1987. Principles for the transfer price
and financial charges for Inga II and the Inga-Shaba line were agreed
during negotiations and SNEL's 1987 accounts wouiid be adjusted on the basis
of that agreement in accordance with accounting practices acceptable to
IDA.
5.05        The financial position of SNEL as of December 31, 1984 and
December 31, 1985 is shown in Table 5.2.
5.06         SNEL's low debt equity ratio at 11/89 for 1984 reflects a
practice by which the Government has financed nearly all infrastructure and
social investments in the power sector.   Once in operation, these assets
have been transferred to SNEL's accounts and the Government has continued
to pay the corresponding debt service.   Budgetary constraints will prevent
the Government from continuing to bear all debt service on SNEL's behalf,
requiring SNEL to assume increasing responsibility for financing power
sector investments.   For 1985, based on the Helios study (para. 5.04),
SNEL's debt equity ratio increased significantly as 30% (Annex 5.4 D(a))

(iii) a timetable for implementing a level payment plan. Submission of the
action program would be a condition of Credit Effectiveness.



-40-
Tariff Level
5.08       Present electricity tariffs (Annex 5.5), last raised in October
1985 (low voltage 20%, medium voltage 33%), and March 1986 (GECAMINES HV.
22%) were adequate to meet SNEL's requirements for operating expenditures,
debt service and capital expenditures only under the arrangement by which
the Government incurred substantial debt service on SNEL's behalf.  On the
basis of SNEL's forecast capital investment program and the requirement
that SNEL self-finance an increasing proportion of this program, financial
projections show that substantial rate increases will be required in the
future   to  prevent  deterioration  of  SNEL's  financial  performance
(para 5.11). Assuming annual local price escalation rates of 25% for 1986,
20% for 1987, 17% for 1988, 15% for 1989-90, and 12% for 1991 and
thereafter, the level of electricity rates in real terms would be higher
each year than the 1986 level and would ultimately reach the level
equivalent to the preliminary estimates of the long-run economic cost of
energy in Zaire in the mid-1990's (para. 6.06).
5.09        A study of SNEL's tariffs carried out by EdF, financed under
CR 1224-ZR (Shaba Power System Rehabilitation Project ) and completed in
mid-1985, recommenied the introduction of marginal cost pricing based on
time-of-day peak/off-peak rates. However, costs had been derived from an
overly optimistic damand forecast and investment program which have since
been revised downward (para. 3.13). The report was reviewed by SNEL, the
Government and IDA, and its recommendations for an inverted block tariff
and differentiation for the interconnected hydro-based and isolated thermal
syetems have been introduced. Additional study of lifeline rates, regional
differentiation and revised LRMC will be determined by an updating study
once the long-term development plan is finalized (paras. 3.13 and 6.06).
Following an exchange of views with IDA, SNEL would promptly implement the
recommendations of the tariff study as agreed under Credit 1224-ZR.
Future Financial Position and Operations
5.10       The projected financial statements of SNEL for the years 1986
through 1992 together with notes and assumptions used in these statements
are shown in Annexes 5.1 through 5.4.  Projected balance sheets for the
years ending December 31, 1986 through 1992 show that the current assets/
current liabilities ratio during these years varies between 1.3 and 2.1.
In the past, this ratio has been very high due to large amounts tied up in
receivables. As mentioned in para. 5.07, efforts are underway to reduce
the level of receivables and the expected results are reflected in the
satisfactory level of the future current ratio. The debt/equity ratio is
projected to rise to 42/58 in 1986 and average 35/65 over 1987-92 which is
an acceptable level.   In 1985, the Government of Zaire initiated the
practice of on-lending to SNEL at a rate of interest exceeding the rate at
which the Government borrows; terms are negotiated on a case-by-base
basis.    As  a  result,  SNEL's  present  borrowings  are  comprised  of
concessional loans (0-2% interest) passed on by the Government with no
supplemental interest plus recently negotiated loans averaging 15 years
repavient at rates of interest varying between 7 and 11 Z per annum.  In



-41-
order to gradually move toward a policy of onlending at commercial terms,
the practice of Government relending of concessional loans should be phased
out, and onlending at a rate exceeding the Government borrowing rate should
be continued. During negotiations, agreement was reached that all grants,
credits and loans obtained by the Government for the purpose of financing
SNEL's 1985-92 investment program would be onlent to SNEL at a rate of
interest of no less than 5%; SNEL would in all cases assume the foreign
exchange risk.
5.11      To meet the future operating and debt service requirements and to
make a reasonable contribution to its construction program from internally
generated funds, SNEL would require timely tariff revisions. Based on the
financial projections detailed in Annex 5.1, rate increases would be
required at the rates of 86%, 24%, 22%, 15%, 15% and 14% respectively from
1987 to 1992. The large rate increase needed in January 1987 is due to the
proposed elimination of Government subsidies (for operation of the SIS and
borrowings on SNEL's behalf (para. 3.14)).  This increase would raise the
average rate from its present level of Z 0.705/kWh (UStI.1/kWh) to Z 1.481/
kWh (UtM2.1/kWh), which is still low compared with other countries of the
region and the estimated LRMC of USt5.0). In view of the magnitude of this
increase, it is recommended that the adjustment be made in phases in line
with Zaire's present economic stabilization and recovery program. For the
remainder of 1986, the Government has approved an average increase of 13Z
taking effect July 1 for commercial LV and MV rates, September 1 for HV
rates and October 1 for residential LV custouers, bringing the new average
rate to Z 0.795/kWh (US tl.3IkWh). In 1987, the 86% increase over the 1986
level will be phased with increases in HV rates in March and September and
LV and MV rates January 1 and July 1. The principle of semi-annual review
and adjustments was agreed with the Government and SNEL during negotiations
to improve SNEL's financial situation and avoid large increases which have
occurred in the past due to delay in approval of adjustments. During
negotiations agreement was obtained that SNEL will take all measures
required including the adjustment of the structure and level of its
tariffs, to produce for each of its fiscal years beginning in 1986, funds
from internal sources equivalent to about 30% of the annual average of
capital expenditures incurred or to be incurred during that year and the
two next following fiscal years; before July in each of its fiscal years
SNEL would, on the basi0 of forecasts satisfactory to IDA review the
adequacy of its tariffs to meet the requirement for cash generation against
capital expenditures and furnish to IDA a copy of the review upon its
completion.
5.12        The projected operations of SNEL indicate that its financial
performance would be satisfactory for the years 1986-92 based on projected
sales and costs and the tariff levels resulting from the proposed covenant
with debt service coverage varying between 1.5 and 2.5 times; the operating
ratio (excluding depreciation) decreasing from 0.59 in 1986 to 0.38 in
1992; and net cash contribution to investment varying between 20% and 33%.

VI. PROJECT JUSTIFICATION AND RISKS
Kivu/Zaire-Rwanda-Burundi Regional Interconnected System Investment Program
6.01       Least Cost Solution.  Construction of the Ruzizi II generating
station is now underway and Zaire is committed to provide one third of the
cost of the project (para. 1.11 and 2.27).   It has also entered into a
contract with SINELAC to purchase sufficient power to cover one third of
the cost of operation, maintenance and debt service, and without the
rehabilitation and extension of the distribution networks in the Kivu area,
Zaire could not distribute power from the generating station and meet the
forecast demand for electricity. The mission has reviewed the consultants'
reports (Annex 7.1) and is in agreement with the recommendation that the
least-cost method for Zaire of meeting the forecast demand in the
Zaire(Kivu)-Rwanda-Burundi interconnected system is by rehabilitating the
Ruzizi I hydroplant in the short-term and rehabilitating and extending the
distribution networks in the Kivu area. The proposed project is a part of
the regional development program.
6.02      Return on Investment.  The economic rate of return on the power
program has been calculated as the discount rate at which the present value
of the capital and operating costs of the program equals the present value
of the incremental benefits, expected from the development program. The
ERR for the regional development program was determined as 8.9Z excluding
consumers' surplus and 13.4% including consumers' surplus, in the Staff
Appraisal Report No. 4303-EAF, dated May 5, 1983.  Based on assumptions
detailed in Annex 6.1, the economic rate of return on the regional
investment program was recomputed to be 8.8%.  By taking into acount the
economic benefit (consumers' surplus) deriving from the availability of
hydropower rather than higher cost diesel generated power which it is
estimated some 15% of consumers would be ready to buy, the economic rate of
return was determined to be 11.5%. In this case benefits for this portion
of sales were based on alternative costs of d'lesel generation (economic
cost of diesel oil in the region estimated at US$600ltonne). The rates of
return have been found to be comparable tn those given in the original
Staff Appraisal Report.  The economic rates of return are sensitive to
changes in costs and revenues. Results are summarized in Table 6.1. The
economic rates of return are acceptable.

Rehabilitation of the Ruzizi I Hydro Power Plant
6.03         Return on Investment. If the existing deficiencies in the
Ruzizi I plant are not remedied soon, total replacement of most of the
electromechanical equipment in a few years would become inevitable. It is
assumed that the costs of such major replacements would amount to roughly
US$500 per installed kW or US$14.1 million (in March 1986) prices. Taking
into account the surplus generating capacity which will exist in the
regionial  interconnected  system until  1992,  replacement  units  of  the
Ruzizi I station would need to be commissioned by this date. The economic
rate of return on the US$7.5 million rehabilitation expenditures (base cost
+ physical contingencies - engineering servic.s including the feasibility
study) proposed under the project would be 21.1%.  This does not account
for any losses from increasingly unreliable operation during the
intervening period.   Details are given in Annex 6.2 and sunmmarized in
Table 6.2. In all cases the economic rates of return are acceptable.

Rehabilitation and Extension of the Distribution Networks in the Kivu Area
6.04      Return on Investment.  The economic rate of return for improving
the capacity and reliability of the distribution system has been calculated
based on added revenues from measured sales. It is estimated that without
rehabilitation, the distribution capacity (estimated to be around 17 MW; 50
GWh/year) would decrease by about 5% per year in the 1987-1991 period. To
make up for the deficit which would result, some of the consumers would
utilize their diesel units.   13/   As th3 effect of this would be to
increase the ERR, these sensitivity runs have not been done and no
13/ As a minimum, those operations (farms, workshops, cottor and tea
factories, etc.) that do have standby diesel units (totaling 1,056 kVA;
850 kW) would have to use them more to make up for the lack of
capacity. It is expected that about 1.7 GWh/year of diesel generation
will be substituted by hydro-based electricity supplied from the
regional interconnected system.

adjustments in the benefits were taken into account for the likely greater
availability  (in  capacity  and  reliability)  of  electricity  through
distribution facilities versus the diesel plant capacity utilization
(maintenance and fuel supply problems and foreign exchange needs for diesel
oil). The project also includes extension of the distribution networks to
a capacity of about 35 MW expected to be reached around year 2000. Net
revenues from the forecast sales were determined using long-term marginal
costs for Kivu  (Annex 6.4).   Based on the foregoing assumptions the
economic rate of return was calculated as 15.6%.   Annex 6.3 contains
details  on  the  foregoing computations  and assumptions.    Results  for
sensitivity studies are summnarized in Table 6.3.   The economic rates of
